TI Evaluation of the impact of DEC treatment on vector infection in the
   program of lymphatic filariasis control in Recife, Brazil
SO ICOPA XI: PROCEEDINGS OF THE 11TH INTERNATIONAL CONGRESS OF PARASITOLOGY
LA English
DT Proceedings Paper
CT 11th International Congress of Parasitology (ICOPA XI)
CY AUG 06-11, 2006
CL Glasgow, SCOTLAND
SP British Soc Parasitol, World Federat Parasitologists
ID HUMAN BLOOD-SAMPLES; WUCHERERIA-BANCROFTI; POOLS
AB Bancroftian filariasis is focally endemic in Recife, a city located on the Northeastern coast of Brazil. Culex quinquefasciatus is the vector responsible for transmission. Although most of the bancroftian filariasis endemic areas in Brazil in the last century are currently considered extinct, Recife still remains as a transmission area, with more than 40.000 infected people. The World Health Organization (WHO) has launched a global program for the elimination of lymphatic filariasis (LF) until 2020 and many country-level elimination strategies are being achieved worldwide. On November 2003, a single course DEC mass treatment was administered to 17.000 individuals from Agua Fria, a district of Recife, where microfilarial (mf) prevalence reached 6,21%. Adult Cx. quinquefasciatus females from houses in that area were collected before and during treatment, in order to monitor vector infection rate and to detect the expected decreasing of microfilaraemia due to the mass drug administration (MDA). A total of 6,409 females mosquitoes were examined. Using PCR we observed a reduction in the vector infection rate from 0.96 % (before treatment) to 0.20 % after the first MDA and 0.0% five months after the second MDA treatment. Thenceforward all the samples collected showed to be negative. These results point out that the control program of filariasis is being effective.

TI Genetic structure of natural populations of Aedes aegypti at the micro-
   and macrogeographic levels in Brazil
SO JOURNAL OF THE AMERICAN MOSQUITO CONTROL ASSOCIATION
LA English
DT Article
DE Aedes aegypti; allozymes; genetic structure; control programs; Brazil
ID DENGUE VIRUS; ENZYMATIC VARIABILITY; ELECTROPHORETIC DATA;
   DIFFERENTIATION; VECTOR; CULICIDAE; DIPTERA; PATTERNS; MOSQUITO
AB Genetic variation in 13 populations of Aedes aegypti from 3 regions of Brazil was compared using variation at 10 isozyme loci. Heterozygosities varied from 0.050 +/- 0.027 to 0.280 +/- 0.120, and a large genetic differentiation (F-ST = 0.144) was observed among all populations. The largest within-regions differences were found between populations from the urban areas of northeast Brazil (F-ST = 0.152). Ecological conditions are likely having an impact on the population structure of Ae. aegypti in the different regions of Brazil.

TI Genetic differentiation of Aedes aegypti (Diptera : Culicidae), the
   major dengue vector in Brazil
SO JOURNAL OF MEDICAL ENTOMOLOGY
LA English
DT Article
DE mosquitoes; genetic variability; random amplified polymorphic DNA;
   population structure
ID AMPLIFIED POLYMORPHIC DNA; RAPD-PCR MARKERS; CHI-MINH CITY;
   POPULATION-GENETICS; BREEDING STRUCTURE; MOSQUITO; NUMBER; FAMILIES;
   DISTANCE; VIRUS
AB In 2000, Brazil reported 180,137 cases of dengue, approximate to80% of the total in the Americas. However, little is known about gene flow among the vector populations in Brazil. Random amplified polymorphic DNA (RAPD) was used to study the genetic structure of Aedes aegypti in 15 populations from five states, with a range extending 2,800 km. An analysis of 47 polymorphic RAPD loci estimated gene flow at the macro- (different states) and micro- (different cities) geographical levels. Genetic polymorphism was high (H-S = 0.274), and high levels of genetic differentiation existed both between different states (G(ST) = 0.317) and between cities or neighborhoods in each state (G(ST) = 0.085- 0.265). These values are higher than those described for any other populations of A.aegypti.

TI Genetic diversity in Brazilian Populations of Aedes albopictus
SO MEMORIAS DO INSTITUTO OSWALDO CRUZ
LA English
DT Article
DE Aedes albopictus; random amplified polymorphic DNA; genetic structure
ID UNITED-STATES; BREEDING STRUCTURE; SKUSE; CULICIDAE; DIPTERA; AMERICA
AB Random amplfied polymorphic DNA (RAPD) analysis technique was undertaken in Aedes albopictus populations from three states in Brazil, Rio de Janeiro (RJ), Minas Gerais (MG) and Pernambuco (PE), to estimate the level of genetic variability and levels of genetic exchange between populations. Allele and genotype frequencies were measured on 47 RAPD loci. Average observed heterozigosity (H) ranged from 0.282 in MG to 0.355 in Casa Forte (PE) population. Genetic distances estimates indicated that RJ and MG were more genetically similar than populations from PE. Genetic variation observed in local Brazilian populations was attributed to genetic draft associated with, restricted gene flow in recently established populations.
